  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6aa72572-87d3-49d5-b7e2-b2847afa04c7'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText4830998780367438536" style="display:none">The power-hungry High Lord of Kalare has launched a rebellion against the aging First Lord, Gaius Sextus, who with the loyal forces of Alera must fight beside the unlikeliest of allies-the equally contentious High Lord of Aquitaine. <br /><br />Meanwhile, young Tavi of Calderon joins a newly formed legion under an assumed name even as the ruthless Kalare unites with the Canim, bestial enemies of the realm whose vast numbers spell certain doom for Alera. <br /><br />When treachery from within destroys the army's command structure, Tavi finds himself leading an inexperienced, poorly equipped legion-the only force standing between the Canim horde and the war-torn realm.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2315379608" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2315379608?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=butcher-jim">butcher-jim</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2315379608" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16658812460577273513">Roman legions rock the Pokemon house. <br/><br/>There seems to be no universal acclaim to the greatness of this series as it´s with behemoths like Sanderson, Rothfuß, Brett, Simmons, Williams,… and I guess one of the reasons for this is that there is nothing really new in this one while people got used to reading one genre revolution after the other. <br/><br/>So we have: The hive mind organism evil enemy, check. A frenemy whose culture is used to describe different societal systems, showing a kind of alternative h</span>
  <span id="freeText16658812460577273513" style="display:none">Roman legions rock the Pokemon house. <br /><br />There seems to be no universal acclaim to the greatness of this series as it´s with behemoths like Sanderson, Rothfuß, Brett, Simmons, Williams,… and I guess one of the reasons for this is that there is nothing really new in this one while people got used to reading one genre revolution after the other. <br /><br />So we have: The hive mind organism evil enemy, check. A frenemy whose culture is used to describe different societal systems, showing a kind of alternative higher future evolution of pack animals, check. The fighting system, a mixture of oldfashioned military discipline with elemental powers.<br /><br />But I would say that this unique mixture of known ideas is something new too, with its complexity, interwoven plot lines, accessibility for readers of any age and simply Butchers´ amazing writing style, he didn´t study creative writing for nothing. <br /><br />For the ones who are searching the next big new thing in fantasy, for one similar to the mentioned authors who break conventions and form subgenres, it might be just an average fantasy series. But for me, it was perfect and if one doesn´t want the next genre revolution, that is very probably dark and gritty, but an entertaining and oldfashioned piece of fast fantasy telling, it´s the pick of choice.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Creator/JimButcher">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/CodexAlera">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="16658812460577273513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2128578242?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2017</a>

        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2128578242" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7126771264140670244">This series just keeps getting better and better. <br/><b>THAT TWIST!</b><br/>I <i>never</i> saw that spoilery thing coming, and I'm betting neither did most of you. But <i>kudos</i> if you did...<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506698787ra/24043889.gif' width='400' height='180' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Ok, it starts out with the stars turning red and <i>something</i> scary getting loose in the clouds...</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506698787ra/24043890.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>All the characters we <b>love</b> are back, along with all the ones we <b>love</b> to <b>hate</b>.<br/><i>*rubs hands together with glee*</i><br/>The story switches mostly between these main groups of characters:<br/>Tavi (and his friends) on a spoilery mission from Gaius as Legiona</span>
  <span id="freeText7126771264140670244" style="display:none">This series just keeps getting better and better. <br><b>THAT TWIST!</b><br>I <i>never</i> saw that spoilery thing coming, and I'm betting neither did most of you. But <i>kudos</i> if you did...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506698787ra/24043889.gif" width="400" height="180" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Ok, it starts out with the stars turning red and <i>something</i> scary getting loose in the clouds...</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506698787ra/24043890.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All the characters we <b>love</b> are back, along with all the ones we <b>love</b> to <b>hate</b>.<br><i>*rubs hands together with glee*</i><br>The story switches mostly between these main groups of characters:<br>Tavi (and his friends) on a spoilery mission from Gaius as Legionaries, which turns into SO much more. &lt;--FANTASTIC STUFF!<br>Then, Bernard and Amara (and their enemies!) on a spoilery mission from Gaius to rescue political prisoners. &lt;--DRAMA &amp; INFIGHTING, BABY!<br>Also, Isana and Fade, who because of spoilery stuff that happens, show the reader both of their origin stories. &lt;--FINALLY!<br>And even though we don't get to see things from her POV, Katai is <i>always</i> on her own personal spoilery mission to save her favorite Aleran from his Aleran stupidity. <br>She's such an unrepentant badass! &lt;--LOVE HER!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492449685ra/22518490.gif" width="400" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anyway, book three really came together into something truly delightful for me. <br>This series? It's made of ink and awesomeness!<br><i>These</i> are the perfect kinds of Fantasy novels for me. I know that not everyone will agree with me (and that's fine!), but I really prefer less <b>gory</b> stuff and more <b>adventure-y</b> stuff in my books. Which makes Jim Butcher's <b>Codex Alera</b> seem kind of tailor-made for me.<br><b>Highly recommended!</b></span>

  <span id="freeText4917841760007942553" style="display:none">[4.5 stars] The Codex Alera is shaping up to becoming one of my favorite fantasy series. It’s already responsible for one of my favorite books I’ve ever read (Academ’s Fury) and I’d be hard-pressed to tell you why Cursor’s Fury doesn’t deserve a spot of honor right next to it. It focused more on the legionary aspect of the story, which brought along with it an excellent mix of battle scenes, intrigue, and character development. I loved absolutely everything about it. I’ve been stingy with solid 5-star ratings lately because I want them to signify an outstanding book and really mean something when I assign them. Cursor’s Fury deserved a 5-star imo, but I kept it at 4.5 because it wasn't my favorite of the series. Good stuff.<br><br>Overall, I’m thrilled with this series and can’t wait to continue on. The first book, Furies of Calderon, was so average I almost didn’t keep reading. <div id="review_1394265342" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1394265342" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1394265342?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1394265342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13012998863994912687">The First Lord of Alera does not get any younger (I am stating obvious, am I not?) He also does not have any male heir - or female for that matter. No wonder that everybody and their brother want his job, yesterday. Several high-ranking people actually have the means to get it. <br/><br/>To neutralize the danger from the most likely contender (High Lord Kalare), The First Lord forces him to act early hoping his lack of preparation would allow for an easy victory. He severely underestimated Kalare's streng</span>
  <span id="freeText13012998863994912687" style="display:none">The First Lord of Alera does not get any younger (I am stating obvious, am I not?) He also does not have any male heir - or female for that matter. No wonder that everybody and their brother want his job, yesterday. Several high-ranking people actually have the means to get it. <br><br>To neutralize the danger from the most likely contender (High Lord Kalare), The First Lord forces him to act early hoping his lack of preparation would allow for an easy victory. He severely underestimated Kalare's strength and ambition. For the third time (fourth if you count the past event which gets mentioned regularly) the realm is in mortal danger. For the third time the regulars of the series have to face overwhelming odds in attempt to salvage an unwinnable situation. <br><br>For every single book of the series I read so far I was sure I would rate it with 3 stars and every one of them ended up with 4, and this time is not an exception. The beginning was fairly boring and I did not expect much from the way the events began. The conflict seemed on the much lesser scale than those of the previous installments. Tavi is still Mary Sue - or Gary Stu in his case - who can do no wrong and can overcome all challenges. I was not impressed with what Isana was doing through the whole book. <br><br>Somewhere as the plot moved along the stakes became huge, the pace picked up and the novel became the expected - at this point - equivalent of a summer blockbuster movie with lots of explosions, big fights, last minute escapes, and other well-known attributes. This means mindless entertainment at (almost) its best. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443457506i/16362706._SX540_.png" width="240" height="120" alt="Blockbuster" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As an icing on the cake we finally get to see some interesting back history of Isana and Tavi. The big plot twist at the end typical for the series is present as well, but this time I was able to predict it (yay for me!)<br><br>I already mentioned 4 stars as the rating. Now that I am half-done with the series it is fairly safe to say I will finish it even if all of the remaining books are abysmal. They are most probably not. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13012998863994912687" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_362649744" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/362649744" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/362649744?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441015474" href="/book/show/504430.Cursor_s_Fury">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-before-goodreads">read-before-goodreads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362649744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17027812953453406240"><b>Executive Summary:</b> To me this is where the series really starts to shine. Mr. Butcher established the world and the key players in the last 2 books, and now he gets down the business of telling the story.<br/><br/><b>Audio book:</b> I didn't like Ms. Reading too much at the start. Her male voices bothered me. By this book however, I couldn't imagine anyone else reading this. There is a scene where random legionaries are calling out and Ms. Reading does different voices for all of them. <br/><br/>I think she's also flushed</span>
  <span id="freeText17027812953453406240" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> To me this is where the series really starts to shine. Mr. Butcher established the world and the key players in the last 2 books, and now he gets down the business of telling the story.<br /><br /><b>Audio book:</b> I didn't like Ms. Reading too much at the start. Her male voices bothered me. By this book however, I couldn't imagine anyone else reading this. There is a scene where random legionaries are calling out and Ms. Reading does different voices for all of them. <br /><br />I think she's also flushed out the voices she uses for all the main and secondary characters to really add that extra something that not all audio books readers seem to manage.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />I was both a bit eager and nervous for this re-read. This is only of only a handful of books that I've given 5 stars to and on my favorites shelf. My memory of it seems to have held up pretty well however.<br /><br />This book seems feels far less trope heavy to me as the last two. You still have your chosen one story, but I was just so wrapped up in the awesomeness of it all that I just didn't spend any thinking about it.<br /><br />The first half of this book is good, but the second half is even better. Unlike the last book where I somewhat dreaded any chapter that took us away from the main story, the secondary stories in this book are much more interesting. Adding a lot of depth to the politics of the world and many of the secondary characters.<br /><br />For a book that focuses mostly on a newly formed legion, there seems to actually be less time spent on battles, which may be a plus or minus for you depending on how much you enjoy reading them. Personally I think he strikes the balance just right and Tavi really shines in this book as a result.<br /><br />No one is going to accuse this of being some deep, complex series full of numerous unexpected twists and turns. However while some of it is pretty predictable, I think Mr. Butcher does manage a few surprises amid the more expected plot developments. But honestly, who cares? I was having far too much fun listening this book to spend much of the review getting into that.<br /><br />Part adventure, part political thriller, part war novel with a decent amount of romance thrown in, there is a likely something for everyone here. I for one had trouble stopping for the day by the end and had to jump right into the next book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17027812953453406240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

All of the other characters have been interesting and compelling all along and continue to be so. It's just hard when the focal character isn't. <br/><br/>Looking forward to the rest of the series. </span>

<div id="review_1835964914" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1835964914" />
    <a title="Rossana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11002007-rossana"><img alt="Rossana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503654186p2/11002007.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11002007-rossana?shelf=best-of-the-best">best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11002007-rossana?shelf=fictional-bf">fictional-bf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11002007-rossana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11002007-rossana?shelf=2016-favs">2016-favs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1835964914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9007295146928748644">THAT ENDING.<br/><br/><br/>Ok, so, I loved this book so much! This was my favorite installment, I loved everything about it: Tavi, the Canim, Tavi, the military setting, Tavi, the new characters, TAVI and basically everything else.<br/>I enjoyed all the flashbacks, I think they are very well done and also necessary to the story. Araris is now a much more relatable character and I got to know Septimus, my new obsession.<br/><br/>But let's talk about the very best: Tavi. Oh God I love you. At the beginning of FoC I liked you a</span>
  <span id="freeText9007295146928748644" style="display:none">THAT ENDING.<br /><br /><br />Ok, so, I loved this book so much! This was my favorite installment, I loved everything about it: Tavi, the Canim, Tavi, the military setting, Tavi, the new characters, TAVI and basically everything else.<br />I enjoyed all the flashbacks, I think they are very well done and also necessary to the story. Araris is now a much more relatable character and I got to know Septimus, my new obsession.<br /><br />But let's talk about the very best: Tavi. Oh God I love you. At the beginning of FoC I liked you and I thought you were great and fun to read about, but now, NOW I can't even find the right words to express my love.<br />Tavi is easily one of my fav characters of 2016, second only to Kip Guile (Sevro au Barca and Dalinar Kholin don't make the list 'cause I've officially met them in 2015...). I love the fact that he's furyless but he doesn't act as a human case and he's not looked down upon because of it: he's very resorceful, loyal, clever, brave, he's the perfect commander and the perfect friend, I just can't wait to see how he will act in the next book, it's going to be epic!<br /><br />Fantasy books heavy on politics and military strategy are easily my favorite, so it doesn't come as a surprise that I gave Cursor's Fury 5 stars. The only thing I didn't find as entertaining as the rest of the book was Amara's plotline: I didn't really care for her and Bernard and Rook, even though I know their story was as important as the others.<br /><br />Anyway, fantastic series! Need to have the next book in my hands ASAP. </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_260944535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260944535" />
    <a title="Kaila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3335221-kaila"><img alt="Kaila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525808775p2/3335221.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/260944535?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaila" href="/user/show/3335221-kaila">Kaila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335221-kaila?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335221-kaila?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335221-kaila?shelf=fantasy-aficionados-challenge-2012">fantasy-aficionados-challenge-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335221-kaila?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer260944535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16463571283896075311">I have yet to actually like any of the books in the Codex Alera. Why do I keep reading them, you ask? Good question. I guess at some point I couldn't tear my eyes away from the train wreck and I love a good groan as well as the next bloke. At this point I'm in gaped mouthed awe at how angry these books make me, and I just have to know if they continue to be so bad. Prepare for maximum bitchiness.<br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I'll begin with the title. Once you figure out the naming scheme for the Codex Alera b</span></span>
  <span id="freeText16463571283896075311" style="display:none">I have yet to actually like any of the books in the Codex Alera. Why do I keep reading them, you ask? Good question. I guess at some point I couldn't tear my eyes away from the train wreck and I love a good groan as well as the next bloke. At this point I'm in gaped mouthed awe at how angry these books make me, and I just have to know if they continue to be so bad. Prepare for maximum bitchiness.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'll begin with the title. Once you figure out the naming scheme for the Codex Alera books, where the series is going becomes pretty obvious. The sixth book is called <i>First Lord's Fury</i>. Damn Jim Butcher, spoiler that shit! At this point I can only hope I'm wrong, but I really do hate nothing more in the world than being spoiled so I'm not going to read the synopsis of the last book to find out. I'll come back and edit when I get there. (EDIT two years later: Yeah...I was right.)<br /><br />For now though, Tavi is a Cursor in the aptly named <i>Cursor's Fury</i>. This is the farmer-turned-savior trope taken to a whole new level, as from the <i>first chapter</i>, Tavi does not go to the First Lord. No no, the First Lord comes to <i>him</i>. Like Tavi is seriously busier than the First Lord? Come on now. And what does Gaius Sextus immediately do? What every good emperor would. Ask about his agent's LOVE LIFE. "Hey Tavi I thought I'd come to see you since you're obviously a busy man, hey by the way how goes shagging the ambassador?" What?! I already cared very little about your abilities as a leader, but now I could not care less that the rest of the book is all about people throwing their lives away to protect YOUR kingdom, when you obviously do not deserve as much. You spent the last book complaining about being overworked, and your brief foray in this book you come personally to give a soldier orders any old servant could have done, thoroughly destroying any sympathy you might have had from me in the process. (EDIT: Yes, I realize that I refused to pick up on the very not subtle hints that Tavi was his grandson. I stand by these statements.)<br /><br />That is what begins what I eventually realize is a complete lack of a chain of command or any sort of military knowledge. Tavi is always able to go directly to the top with no repercussions. True, this is not a modern day army, but if there was ever an army that loved discipline, duty, and knowing your place, it was the Romans. He can waltz into the general's tent and no one bats an eyelid, even though we're the only ones who are supposed to know he's not <i>actually</i> that low on the totem pole. He is placed as a logistics officer, assisting in keeping the army running smoothly, well geared, and well fed. This is a RUSE so that we are cowed into believing one iota of thought went into how a army is run. He is sent to go buy grain off local farms but as SOON as the battle started, the problem of feeding the army was never mentioned again. "An army marches on its stomach" is a saying for a reason, and supply lines are serious business when it comes to defending a town. They're never mentioned.<br /><br />Then, HOW CONVENIENT, the entire officer's corps is wiped out. WHOEVER WILL SAVE US?! Thank God one officer wasn't there. Yes, TAVI TO THE RESCUE. At this point, he has only been in school for two years, and he's going up against soldiers, sometimes with years of battle experience, and they just shrug it off and say, "Boy is that kid clever." He manages to come up with several deus ex machina; particularly I'm thinking of the Knights Aeris bending light to make a gigantic lens of fiery death. No one has ever thought of this before? Seriously, you left it up to the kid with no furies? Any battle that does not employ this tactic from now on is wasting lives. And I'm positive the world is going to pretend like it never happened, and this innovation will be forgotten. If it does continue to get used, I'll eat my words, but there's basically nothing an army can do against that, which doesn't make for very interesting battles. (EDIT: I was right. It's never mentioned again.)<br /><br />Let's take a look at how the battle was laid out. I never fully understood it, and even after looking at the Butcher <a href="http://www.jim-butcher.com/posts/2009/codex-alera-map" rel="nofollow noopener">approved map</a> over at his website, it made even less sense. The entire battle was over a city that spanned two sides of a river, and the bridge connecting the two. Based on the map, you can see the town, Elinarch, over on the western side. Ok. Let's think about this. The Canim had a fleet that was hundreds of ships, and they all landed in the same place. Let's make our best estimate and say it's about 50,000 troops because I can't find anywhere that says how many it was. They all make landfall in Founderport, to the southwest, and they all head for Elinarch. That bridge doesn't even look that important to me, especially because it's to the north, when everything important to the kingdom is to the east. Now, why, WHY, if they really wanted the bridge, couldn't they have landed half the forces up the coast 50 miles, and surrounded the town? Or send a few thousand troops up river 10 miles, so that they can cross over and start attacking the other side? Maybe mess up those supply lines that didn't exist? It is even mentioned at one point that directly below the bridge, Canim troops try to swim across, but are thwarted by a defense Tavi put there. So...go a mile up river where that defense doesn't exist? I simply don't understand. The entire battle was completely useless because the Canim obviously should have won. Of course I want the good guys to win, but if the only reason they did so was because of a bad setting and bad writing, then the victory is senseless.<br /><br />The women...ah the women. I don't like any of them. Kitai is barely ok, but the whole "bonding" thing with Tavi completely turned me off her. How about Isana, who doomed who knows how many soldiers to death because she selfishly chose to only help Fade? And she is busy healing him for literally over a month, the entire time a battle raging a mere mile from her apartment. Seriously, there are so many things wrong with that picture. Isana gets absolutely no sympathy from me ever again. The needs of the many outweigh the needs of the few, that's just how it is.<br /><br />Certain things started to annoy me so much I thought about keeping a scoreboard of how many times I rolled my eyes. The word "crow" shows up 132 times, according to my Kindle search, including all instances of "crowspawn" and "crowbegotten," and this book is only 450 pages. That's a crow at least every three pages. I HATE the word crow SO MUCH now. I seriously never want to read or hear it again. Everybody has flashes of insight, instinct, intuition, and amazing eyesight to see movement out of the corner of their eyes so they can roll away at the last second. If there's a swordsman, he will always be "the best" or "one of the best" in the realm. All the women arch their back whenever their kissed, and Bernard always kisses Amara on the eyes and "full on the mouth." UGH.<br /><br />I was interested in discovering why Tavi has no furies until we actually do find out, and that was a major let down.<br /><br />For the first time, I could not find any redeeming features in this book. The best thing about it is that it is very readable. I openly admit to not being a fan of the first two installments, and this book is more of the same, but even worse. There are so many good fantasy series out there, don't waste your time on this one. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="16463571283896075311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Tom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7476704-tom"><img alt="Tom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333052331p2/7476704.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/514788984?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom" href="/user/show/7476704-tom">Tom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer514788984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14949237655726024798">Another 5 for sure on this book in the series! I’m not sure whether I liked it as much as the second book but I do know that I loved it.<br/><br/>I loved that this book takes place years after the last book and that gives the characters to grow up a bit. As in the other books in the series, there are constant twists and turns. The characters are so real and the villians again show to be in a very grey zone. I love how Gaius is supposed to be the “good” guy but the story is always bringing up evidence that</span>
  <span id="freeText14949237655726024798" style="display:none">Another 5 for sure on this book in the series! I’m not sure whether I liked it as much as the second book but I do know that I loved it.<br /><br />I loved that this book takes place years after the last book and that gives the characters to grow up a bit. As in the other books in the series, there are constant twists and turns. The characters are so real and the villians again show to be in a very grey zone. I love how Gaius is supposed to be the “good” guy but the story is always bringing up evidence that he could easily be portrayed as the villain, especially when it comes to Isana and Amara, and now Tavi and Isana. There are some pretty big revelations that really push the series forward.<br /><br />If you like fantasy and don’t need sex in the story, get into this series!! It is so good! What I like most about the series so far is that they are standalone books that build on the previous one. Instead of a cliffhanger that makes you have to read the next one right away to finish the story it dangles a carrot of info that makes you want to get back to it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14949237655726024798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15504345110372976834">This is the third book in the Codex Alera series by Jim Butcher. This is fantasy in the way that only Jim Butcher can do. This book was a solid 4 stars for me. The ending was 5 stars. I loved the ending. <br/><br/>I like the characters. They are endearing. Even the token romance between Tavi and Katai is kind of sweet, but in a good way. I like that they are still their own character without the constant mooning over each other and plus, she was funny.   <span id="freeText15504345110372976834" style="display:none">This is the third book in the Codex Alera series by Jim Butcher. This is fantasy in the way that only Jim Butcher can do. This book was a solid 4 stars for me. The ending was 5 stars. I loved the ending. <br /><br />I like the characters. They are endearing. Even the token romance between Tavi and Katai is kind of sweet, but in a good way. I like that they are still their own character without the constant mooning over each other and plus, she was funny. There was actually way more to this story than romance. There were even a few other romances happening as well, but it was by no means over done. I loved how all the subplots were mingled together.<br /><br />The action is well written in the battle scenes. There was great movement and detail in this. This turned out to be such a page turner. I didn't want to put it down. So on to book #4.</span>

<div id="review_1676845177" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1676845177" />
    <a title="Tilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42116250-tilly"><img alt="Tilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449007147p2/42116250.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1676845177?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tilly" href="/user/show/42116250-tilly">Tilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42116250-tilly?shelf=age-adult">age-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42116250-tilly?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1676845177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11104256680621530198">This book is my least favorite in the "Codex Alera" series so far and, to be fair, it´s probably mostly my own fault. First of all, it´s been a while since I´ve read the second book in the series and due two the huge amount of characters and place names, which many adult fantasy books feature, I already forgot quite a few and it took me a while to dive into this world again. Furthermore I was a bit disappointed that all the Marat, except for Kitai, were not really present in this book because th</span>
  <span id="freeText11104256680621530198" style="display:none">This book is my least favorite in the "Codex Alera" series so far and, to be fair, it´s probably mostly my own fault. First of all, it´s been a while since I´ve read the second book in the series and due two the huge amount of characters and place names, which many adult fantasy books feature, I already forgot quite a few and it took me a while to dive into this world again. Furthermore I was a bit disappointed that all the Marat, except for Kitai, were not really present in this book because their culture was probably my favorite aspect of the previous two books. I also had some minor problems with the pacing and the way how the chapters were divided up. I would have to switch a bit more between the POV characters instead reading some any successive chapters by the same narrator. Although I like Tavi as a character I found his story line in this book a bit exhausting after a while and sometimes I wished to read a bit more about Bernard and Amara. A very interesting addition to their part of the story to me was Gaelle aka Rook. I´m all in for morally grey characters and their redemption arcs so I had a lot of fun reading about her. Although I already said that I wasn´t blown away by Tavi´s plot line in this book, that doesn´t mean that I like him less as a character. I still think that he is a very believable protagonist and I´m also all in for characters of physical weakness who are able become strong in their own way, so I like the fact that he falls into this category. The chapters about Isana and Fade were also interesting at times and I liked that we got to know more of their backstory. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Nevertheless, I´m not really sure how I feel about the reveal that Isana, who is supposed to be Tavi´s aunt but raised him like a mother IS actually his mother. I would like to get a few more information about it because at this point I don´t really see that so many people should believe that Tavi is her nephew when it wasn´t a secret before that Isana was pregnant. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Overall, it was enjoyable read and, as I said, the reasons why I didn´t enjoy this book as much as its predecessors are mainly personal. I hope to read the next book in the series as soon as possible to make it easier for myself to dive into the world of Alera again. 3.5 of 5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11104256680621530198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Of Butcher's two series, I think I like this series more (even though the Dresden books are a ton of fun). So far, each successive installment has been better than the previous one and I hope the trend continues. Highly Recommended!! </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5049442-soo?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3182076740" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer5386832616807062878">Mini-Review: <br/><br/>4.5 Stars for Narration by Kate Reading<br/>4.5 Stars for Progression & Characters<br/><br/>The series is not about sunshine & roses but I'm a fan of how love for family, friends & lovers are a central part of the story line. I've enjoyed each book in Codex Alera. Cursor's Fury had the best mix of relevant story parts, character & story progression, tension filled action sequences and little moments of connection. <br/><br/>It is a little cheesy? <br/>A little predictable? <br/>Sure. <br/><br/>It's not about a story having bee</span>
  <span id="freeText5386832616807062878" style="display:none">Mini-Review: <br /><br />4.5 Stars for Narration by Kate Reading<br />4.5 Stars for Progression &amp; Characters<br /><br />The series is not about sunshine &amp; roses but I'm a fan of how love for family, friends &amp; lovers are a central part of the story line. I've enjoyed each book in Codex Alera. Cursor's Fury had the best mix of relevant story parts, character &amp; story progression, tension filled action sequences and little moments of connection. <br /><br />It is a little cheesy? <br />A little predictable? <br />Sure. <br /><br />It's not about a story having been done before or making a story a shocking surprise. A great story will sweep you up into the world and characters. Whether you know what is going to happen or not, you will be more invested in seeing it unfold than letting your brain smash up the plot. It's that wild ride where you willingly go with the flow and enjoy the journey from start to finish. I'm really happy to have had that kind of reading adventure with this novel. =)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15417377673206364655"><i>
  <b> 4.5 of 5 stars<br/><br/>-----</b>
</i><br/><br/><br/>I know I've said it a lot of times before but I'll say it again: Tavi is just so damn good and I loved him so much! He proved his skills, cleverness, resourcefulness and courage once more in this book. I can no longer picture the small teenage Tavi herding sheeps and gargants in his steadholt many years ago.   <span id="freeText15417377673206364655" style="display:none"><i>
  <b> 4.5 of 5 stars<br /><br />-----</b>
</i><br /><br /><br />I know I've said it a lot of times before but I'll say it again: Tavi is just so damn good and I loved him so much! He proved his skills, cleverness, resourcefulness and courage once more in this book. I can no longer picture the small teenage Tavi herding sheeps and gargants in his steadholt many years ago. All I can see is a young man, who managed to catch up with his delayed growth spurt, able to lead and commandeer an entire legion to manipulate and outwit their enemies. Though being furycrafted is obviously a serious matter for him and for everyone, it honestly didn't bother me anymore if he's furyless. I mean, furyless or not, his brain is his best asset and he's clearly more capable than anyone around him. I'll give anything just to see his trademark wide grin whenever a slyly clever idea comes to his mind. I can't trade a smart main character for anything else! <br /><br />I've always wanted a very intense battle and I was able to achieved it once more! There were different battles to fight in this book and even as intense as the others but Tavi's battle was my favorite. Always. It always kept me on the edge of my seat! No. The whole book kept me on the edge of my seat the whole freaking time! <br /><br />I think this series already proved its remarkable quality. The content, both plot and character building, continued its consistency to offer an intense build-up to the story. The ending and that spoiler-y twist?? OH! MY! GOD! It didn't cross my mind, even for just a second! And that epilogue part opened a lot of possible events to happen in the future! I'm already itching to read the next book!</span>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118617976?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicholas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicholas" href="/user/show/1072527-nicholas">Nicholas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118617976" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14280682127849979334">Good, good, good book. Tavi is growing up, and his mysterious past, and why he has no furies is finally revealed. <br/><br/>Things that are really good: <br/>1. Maximus<br/>2. Maximus<br/>3. Grown-up Ehren<br/>4. Kitai<br/>5. Tavi as a legionnaire captain<br/><br/>oh wait, .5. The Freaking Canim.<br/><br/>Finally Tavi's got some worthy adversaries and while treachery is always afoot in the Kingdom of Alera, this time, there's far more open conflict. Butcher continues to write really well and put his characters through legitimately believable emotion</span>
  <span id="freeText14280682127849979334" style="display:none">Good, good, good book. Tavi is growing up, and his mysterious past, and why he has no furies is finally revealed. <br /><br />Things that are really good: <br />1. Maximus<br />2. Maximus<br />3. Grown-up Ehren<br />4. Kitai<br />5. Tavi as a legionnaire captain<br /><br />oh wait, .5. The Freaking Canim.<br /><br />Finally Tavi's got some worthy adversaries and while treachery is always afoot in the Kingdom of Alera, this time, there's far more open conflict. Butcher continues to write really well and put his characters through legitimately believable emotional turmoil and growth in a completely fantastic setting filled with awesome imagery and novel twists on epic action.<br /><br />There's nothing not to like about this book, and the way Butcher puts it together makes you feel rewarded for sticking with the series. Questions about key characters' dubious past lives are revealed and the political intrigue gets far thicker and stickier. A perfect example of how one can write really awesome adventure fiction and still be incredibly intelligent. I can't help but compare this series to the Ender series. And every time I do, I think, Butcher wins. This is what Ender should have been after the first book. Card's geopolitical fantasies are an unrealistic shadow compared to the world of Alera. On to the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14280682127849979334" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2106250069" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2106250069" />
    <a title="Kostas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas"><img alt="Kostas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554812738p2/25638423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2106250069?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kostas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kostas" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas">Kostas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441015474" href="/book/show/504430.Cursor_s_Fury">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=epic-high-fantasy">epic-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=military-sff">military-sff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2106250069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15150307544920178861">8.5/10<br/><br/>Reaching at the end of the first half, having earned after two successful books a big recognition both through his writing capabilities and the love of readers who pushed his career even further, Jim Butcher comes to <i>Cursor’s Fury</i>, the third installment of the Codex Alera series, with a greater will and imagination, taking us into a civil war, into a story of <i>Legionaries</i> and Cursors, of political rivals, spies and bestial ritualists, and into an adventure of subjugation and domination, of </span>
  <span id="freeText15150307544920178861" style="display:none">8.5/10<br /><br />Reaching at the end of the first half, having earned after two successful books a big recognition both through his writing capabilities and the love of readers who pushed his career even further, Jim Butcher comes to <i>Cursor’s Fury</i>, the third installment of the Codex Alera series, with a greater will and imagination, taking us into a civil war, into a story of <i>Legionaries</i> and Cursors, of political rivals, spies and bestial ritualists, and into an adventure of subjugation and domination, of loyalty and duty, and of respect and honor, which will divide the realm and its people as never before.<br /><br />Almost three years have passed since the invasion at the heart of the Realm, and the pandemonium that it brought along; a bloody battle that endangered their very existence, leaving behind nothing but souls full of suffering and pain, but now, with the events having become just bad memories, the life for the people of Alera has returned once more back to its normal rhythms- and for Tavi, having completed his training term at the Academy, eager to take on his first mission as an agent of the Crown, these years have given him more free time than he’d had ever wished.<br />Sent in Amaranth Vale, at the ruins of Appia, to fill his time, Tavi has spent the better part of the last six months in Maestro Magnus’s company, assisting him in his discoveries at solving the mysteries of the puzzling technologies of their forefathers.<br />However, with the political climate becoming hotter and hotter lately, as he, Max, and Maestro Magnus will be ordered to join the newly formed First Aleran Legion - having only a little time to adapt to the military life of the <i>legenionares</i> - when an unexplained event decimates their commanding leadership at the worst possible moment, and an old rival emerges from his best friend’s past with the only desire to put him out of the way once and for all, Tavi along with his young, inexperienced and ill-equipped comrades will find themselves against their greatest challenge, face-to-face with a bestial horde and the Realm’s certain doom.<br /><br />At the other end of the Realm, at the fortress of Garrison, Amara, having now accepted the feelings of her heart, has been trying to share them with Bernard even though their obligations seem only to keep growing, desiring nothing more than to start their own little family.<br />But, as they’ll arrive in the city of Ceres - one of the greatest cities in the Realm, hosting from high nobles to esteemed politicians - for Bernard’s family reunion, and to bring to light the true events of the past years before them, when a group of seemingly mad slaves cause chaos, killing the guests one by one, they will soon be faced with their very survival; an adventure that, when Lord Kalarus reveals his intentions for power, she and Bernard will have to undertake a high-risk mission that could very easily destroy everything they have built so far.<br />At the same time, Isana, lost in the memories of her past and the secrets she kept buried deep inside her heart for twenty years, where no one would be able to find them and exploit them, when Fade - her loyal slave and protector - gets mortally wounded beyond any healing, she’ll have to dig up something she had sacrificed long ago in order to save him; meanwhile, Ehren, taking up his first undercover mission in the Sunset Isles, working as a scribe for a fencer, when he falls onto a pirate and his mercenary crew he’ll discover something so indescribable that could judge the fate of all of them.<br /><br />Yet, with the political climate reaching its peak, when the power-hungry Lord Kalarus sends his mercenary forces that he’d gathered over the years at the gates of the city of Ceres, bringing a rebellion against the Crown and the First Lord’s government, and the merciless Canim leader and his ritualists set at the same time their own plans for their dominance, Tavi and the <i>legionnaires</i> of the First Aleran, Amara and Bernard, and Isana and Ehren, will have to take on their missions amidst these difficult time with courage, because if they fail to keep their morale high, it may well bring to the end the dreams of the families and the lives as they’d imagined them.<br /><br />With the second book of the series, <i>Academ’s Fury</i>, to have played an important role in deepening the world-building and the characters, setting the base of the political system, and of the alliances and the rivalries of the High Lords, Jim Butcher comes in <i>Cursor’s Fury</i> with an even greater scope in his imagination, traveling us far away to the western cities of the Realm, which, governed under their lords’ desires and whims, reveal how different they can be to one another through the rules that their people endure, but also at the impact it has on their families, their homes and the control of their living conditions; as well as to the borders between Alera and the land of the Canim, immersing us a little deeper in the ways of their bestial race, and their castes - divided in its warriors, its raiders and its ritualists - that shows their diversity among their ambitious leaders and their acolytes, and their regular warriors and their kin.<br /><br />And, with each book managing to bring an even stronger handling in the development of the plot and of the characters, proving again the extent of his writing capabilities, as well as his desire from the beginning for something more epic, Butcher brings us deep into a great civil war, dividing the Realm between the power-hungry High Lords and the simple people, taking us into a military story of <i>Legionares</i>, Cursors, spies, and politicians, and into an adventure of loyalty, honor, and absolute subjugation, full of battles of suspense and thrill, creating the most entertaining novel in the series yet, but also leaving at the end and many threads open to await eagerly for the sequel and the answers it holds.<br /><br />All in all, <i>Cursor’s Fury</i> is a strong book, with Jim Butcher - coming with a greater will - to takes us, through a civil war, into a military story of <i>Legionares</i> and Cursors, creating a thrilling and moving adventure of honor and loyalty, and of duty and respect that brings the series to a higher level than before, but also leaving us hanging in suspense for the sequel and the next adventures of our favorite characters.<br /><br /><br />Ελληνική κριτική:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Φτάνοντας στο τέλος του πρώτου μισού, έχοντας κερδίσει μετά από δύο επιτυχημένα βιβλία μια μεγάλη αναγνώριση τόσο μέσα από τις συγγραφικές του ικανότητες όσο και την αγάπη των αναγνωστών που ώθησαν την καριέρα του ακόμη περισσότερο, ο Jim Butcher έρχεται στο <i>Cursor’s Fury</i>, το τρίτο μέρος της σειράς Codex Alera, με μια μεγαλύτερη θέληση και φαντασία, πηγαίνοντάς μας μέσα ένα εμφύλιο πόλεμο, μέσα σε μια ιστορία <i>Λεγεωνάριων</i> και Δρομέων, πολιτικών αντίζηλων, κατασκόπων και ζωωδών τυπολατρών, και σε μια περιπέτεια υποδούλωσης και κυριαρχίας, αφοσίωσης και καθήκοντος, και σεβασμού και τιμής, που θα διχάσει το βασίλειο και τους ανθρώπους του όπως ποτέ πριν.<br /><br />Σχεδόν τρία χρόνια έχουν περάσει από την εισβολή στην καρδιά του Βασιλείου, και το πανδαιμόνιο που έφερε μαζί• μια αιματηρή μάχη που διακινδύνευσε την ίδια τους την ύπαρξη, αφήνοντας πίσω τίποτα παρά ψυχές γεμάτες βάσανα και πόνο, αλλά τώρα, με τα γεγονότα να έχουν γίνει μονάχα κακές αναμνήσεις, η ζωή για τους ανθρώπους της Alera έχει γυρίσει για άλλη μια φορά πίσω στους φυσιολογικούς ρυθμούς - και για τον Tavi, έχοντας ολοκληρώσει την εκπαιδευτική του περίοδο στην Ακαδημία, ανυπομονώντας να αναλάβει την πρώτη του αποστολή σαν πράκτορας του Στέμματος, αυτά τα χρόνια του έχουν δώσει περισσότερο ελεύθερο χρόνο απ’ ότι θα επιθυμούσε ποτέ του.<br />Σταλμένος στην Αμάραντη Κοιλάδα, στα ερείπια της Appia, για να γεμίσει τον χρόνο του, ο Tavi έχει περάσει το μεγαλύτερο μέρος των τελευταίων έξι μηνών στην συντροφιά του Μαέστρο Magnus, βοηθώντας τον στις ανακαλύψεις του στο να λύσει τα μυστήρια των αινιγματωδών τεχνολογιών των προπατόρων τους.<br />Ωστόσο, με το πολιτικό κλίμα να γίνεται όλο και πιο καυτό τον τελευταίο καιρό, καθώς αυτός, ο Max και ο Μαέστρο Magnus θα διαταχτούν να ενταχθούν στην νεοσύστατη Πρώτη Αλέρια Λεγεώνα - έχοντας μονάχα λίγο χρόνο για να προσαρμοστούν στην στρατιωτική ζωή των <i>λεγεωνάριων</i> - όταν ένα ανεξήγητο συμβάν αποδεκατίσει την διοικητική ηγεσία τους στην χειρότερη δυνατή στιγμή, και ένας παλιός αντίζηλος αναδυθεί από το παρελθόν του καλύτερού του φίλου με την μόνη επιθυμία να τον βγάλει από την μέση μια και καλή, ο Tavi μαζί με τους νεαρούς, άπειρους και κακοεξοπλισμένους συντρόφους του θα βρεθούν ενάντια με την μεγαλύτερη πρόκλησή τους, πρόσωπο με πρόσωπο με μια ζωώδη ορδή και την σίγουρη καταδίκη του Βασιλείου.<br /><br />Στην άλλη άκρη του Βασιλείου, στο φρούριο του Garrison, η Amara, έχοντας πλέον αποδεχτεί τα αισθήματα της καρδιάς της, αυτά τα τελευταία χρόνια έχει προσπαθήσει να τα μοιραστεί με τον Bernard ακόμη κι αν οι υποχρεώσεις τους φαίνονται μονάχα να συνεχίζουν να πληθαίνουν, επιθυμώντας όσο τίποτε άλλο παρά να ξεκινήσουν την δικιά τους μικρή οικογένεια.<br />Όμως, καθώς θα φτάσουν στην πόλη της Ceres - μια από τις μεγαλύτερες πόλεις του Βασιλείου, φιλοξενώντας από υψηλούς ευγενείς μέχρι αξιότιμους πολιτικούς - για την οικογενειακή επανένωση του Bernard, και για να φέρουν στο φως τα αληθινά γεγονότα των προηγούμενων χρόνων ενώπιόν τους, όταν μια ομάδα φαινομενικών τρελών σκλάβων προκαλέσει ένα χάος, σκοτώνοντας τους καλεσμένους έναν προς έναν, θα βρεθούν σύντομα αντιμέτωποι με την ίδια τους την επιβίωση• μια περιπέτεια που, όταν ο Άρχοντας Kalarus αποκαλύψει τις προθέσεις του για εξουσία, αυτή και ο Bernard θα πρέπει να αναλάβουν μια υψηλού κινδύνου αποστολή που θα μπορούσε πολύ εύκολα να καταστρέψει όλα όσα έχτισαν μέχρι τώρα.<br />Συγχρόνως, η Isana, χαμένη στις αναμνήσεις του παρελθόντος της και των μυστικών που κράτησε θαμμένα βαθιά μέσα στην καρδιά της για είκοσι χρόνια, εκεί όπου κανείς δεν θα μπορούσε να τα βρει και να τα εκμεταλλευτεί, όταν ο Fade - ο πιστός σκλάβος και προστάτης της - πληγωθεί θανάσιμα πέρα από κάθε γιατρειά, θα πρέπει να ξεθάψει κάτι που είχε θυσιάσει πολύ καιρό πριν προκειμένου να τον σώσει• εν τω μεταξύ, ο Ehren, αναλαμβάνοντας την πρώτη του μυστική αποστολή στις Νήσους του Ηλιοβασιλέματος, δουλεύοντας σαν γραφέας για έναν κλεπταποδόχο, όταν πέσει πάνω σε έναν πειρατή και το μισθοφορικό πλήρωμά του θα ανακαλύψει κάτι τόσο απερίγραπτο που θα μπορούσε να κρίνει την μοίρα όλων τους.<br /><br />Κι όμως, με το πολιτικό κλίμα να φτάνει στο αποκορύφωμά του, όταν ο πεινασμένος για εξουσία Άρχοντας Kalarus στείλει τις μισθοφορικές δυνάμεις που συγκέντρωσε με τα χρόνια προς τις πύλες της πόλης της Ceres, φέρνοντας μια επανάσταση ενάντια του Στέμματος και τις κυβέρνησης του Πρώτου Άρχοντα, και ο ανηλεής αρχηγός των Canim και οι τυπολάτρες του θέσουν ταυτόχρονα τα δικά τους σχέδια για την κυριαρχία τους, ο Tavi και οι <i>λεγεωνάριοι</i> της Πρώτης Αλέριας, η Amara και ο Bernard, και η Isana και ο Ehren, θα πρέπει να αναλάβουν τις αποστολές τους εν μέσω αυτής της δύσκολης εποχής με θάρρος, γιατί αν δεν καταφέρουν να κρατήσουν το ηθικό τους υψηλά, μπορεί κάλλιστα να φέρει στο τέλος τα όνειρα των οικογενειών και των ζωών όπως τα είχαν φανταστεί.<br /><br />Με το δεύτερο βιβλίο της σειράς, <i>Academ’s Fury</i>, να έχει παίξει ένα σημαντικό ρόλο στην εμβάθυνση της κοσμοπλασία και των χαρακτήρων, θέτοντας την βάση του πολιτικού συστήματος, και των συμμαχιών και των αντιζηλιών των Υψηλών Αρχόντων, ο Jim Butcher έρχεται στο <i>Cursor’s Fury</i> με μια ακόμη μεγαλύτερη βλέψη στην φαντασία του, ταξιδεύοντάς μας μακριά στις δυτικές πόλεις του Βασιλείου, οι οποίες, κυβερνούμενες κάτω από τις επιθυμίες και τις ιδιοτροπίες των αρχόντων τους, αποκαλύπτουν το πόσο διαφορετικές μπορεί να είναι η μία με την άλλη μέσα από τους κανόνες που οι άνθρωποί τους υπομένουν, αλλά και στην επίπτωση που έχει πάνω στις οικογένειες, στα σπίτια τους, και στον έλεγχο της διαβίωσής τους• όπως επίσης και στα σύνορα μεταξύ της Alera και της χώρας των Canim, βυθίζοντάς μας λίγο βαθύτερα στους τρόπους της ζωώδης φυλής τους, και των κοινωνικών τάξεών τους - χωρισμένες στους πολεμιστές, τους επιδρομείς και τους τυπολάτρες τους - που μας δείχνει την διαφορετικότητα ανάμεσα στους φιλόδοξους αρχηγούς τους και τους ακόλουθων ιερέων τους, και στους κανονικούς πολεμιστές και τους συγγενών τους.<br /><br />Και, με κάθε βιβλίο να καταφέρνει να φέρνει ένα ακόμη δυνατότερο χειρισμό στην ανάπτυξη της πλοκή και των χαρακτήρων, αποδεικνύοντας ξανά την έκταση των συγγραφικών ικανοτήτων του, όπως επίσης και την επιθυμία του από την αρχή για κάτι πιο επικό, ο Butcher μας φέρνει βαθιά μέσα σε ένα μεγάλο εμφύλιο πόλεμο, χωρίζοντας το Βασίλειο μεταξύ τους πεινασμένους για εξουσία Υψηλούς Άρχοντες και τους απλούς ανθρώπους, πηγαίνοντάς μας μέσα σε μια στρατιωτική ιστορία <i>Λεγεωνάριων</i>, Δρομέων, κατασκόπων, και πολιτικών, και σε μια περιπέτεια αφοσίωσης, τιμής, και απόλυτης υποδούλωσης, γεμάτη με μάχες αγωνίας και συγκίνησης, δημιουργώντας το πιο ψυχαγωγικό μυθιστόρημα στην σειρά ακόμη, αλλά και αφήνοντας στο τέλος και πολλά νήματα ανοιχτά για να περιμένουμε ανυπόμονα για την συνέχεια και τις απαντήσεις που κρατάει.<br /><br />Όλα για όλα, το <i>Cursor’s Fury</i> είναι ένα δυνατό βιβλίο, με τον Jim Butcher - ερχόμενος με μια μεγαλύτερη θέληση - να μας πηγαίνει, μέσω ενός εμφύλιου πολέμου, μέσα σε μια στρατιωτική ιστορία <i>Λεγεωνάριων</i> και Δρομέων, δημιουργώντας μια συναρπαστική και συγκινητική περιπέτεια τιμής και αφοσίωσης, και καθήκοντος και σεβασμού που φέρνει την σειρά σε ένα υψηλότερο επίπεδο από πριν, αλλά και αφήνοντάς μας να κρεμόμαστε σε αγωνία για την συνέχεια και τις επόμενες περιπέτειες των αγαπημένων μας χαρακτήρων.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_185096870" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/185096870" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/185096870?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780441015474" href="/book/show/504430.Cursor_s_Fury">review of another edition</a>

<div id="review_2880230677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2880230677" />
    <a title="Nadine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3759963-nadine"><img alt="Nadine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566849081p2/3759963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2880230677?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadine" href="/user/show/3759963-nadine">Nadine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781841497464" href="/book/show/4961955-cursor-s-fury">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2880230677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3959631530125275346">Cursor’s Fury is the third installment in the Codex Alera. Its main focus is war. For most of the novel, readers follow the various characters as a full-fledged war is fought against the Canim.<br/><br/>Tavi is now much older and readers get to see who he is as a man and what he’s capable of despite his limitations. Tavi is intelligent and adaptable. Both qualities serve him well as he fights on the front lines.<br/><br/>Max is easily one of my favorite secondary characters. He’s fun as he brings a lot of comedy to</span>
  <span id="freeText3959631530125275346" style="display:none">Cursor’s Fury is the third installment in the Codex Alera. Its main focus is war. For most of the novel, readers follow the various characters as a full-fledged war is fought against the Canim.<br /><br />Tavi is now much older and readers get to see who he is as a man and what he’s capable of despite his limitations. Tavi is intelligent and adaptable. Both qualities serve him well as he fights on the front lines.<br /><br />Max is easily one of my favorite secondary characters. He’s fun as he brings a lot of comedy to the scenes he’s in. Though, he’s also a very capable soldier and seeing him in action made me appreciate him all the more.<br /><br />Butcher had me worried about Amara as a character. Her relationship with Barnard is not sanctioned by law since passing on the ability to furycraft to the next generation is required. Amara is barren making their relationship illegal. I was worried Butcher would relegate her character to the female obsessed with getting pregnant and having kids. Fortunately, Amara is just as badass as she started off in the first novel if not more. There’s a particular escape/pursuit sequence that she crushes with her awesomeness.<br /><br />Isana’s chapters are generally not my favorite compared to the others, though that’s not to say I dislike her or her story. In this novel, Isana shines as readers get a well-deserved glimpse into the past. These scenes are full of answers while also posing new ones for readers to ponder. There’s a particular scene that’s heartbreaking yet beautiful. Butcher’s writing in that chapter is easily some of his best as he hits all the emotional notes with ease.<br /><br />The only criticism I have of Cursor’s Fury is the lack of Kitai. She pops in and out of the novel at convenient times where her expertise is needed. This may be in part due to how overpowered she is, but I was really looking forward to exploring her link with Tavi further.<br /><br />Overall, Cursor’s Fury packs a punch with its twists and turns coupled with reveals that change the direction of the story in interesting and unexpected ways.'<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Tavi can furycraft!!! And so can Kitai?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="3959631530125275346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
